## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of state (x, v) and possibly time t, which is the standard first-order form of an oscillator equation. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators commonly combine a restoring force term depending on x, damping depending on v, and optional external/parametric forcing depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring acceleration)
- Linear damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Forced linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (external periodic forcing)
- Nonlinear stiffness (Duffing, cubic spring): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos-capable forced oscillator)
- Pendulum equation (small-to-large angle): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (nonlinear restoring via sine of angle/position)
- Van der Pol oscillator (Liénard type): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v + c2 * x (self-excited nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v + c2 * x (negative damping at small |v|, limit cycle)
- Quadratic/cubic drag damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like nonlinear damping)
- Nonlinear damping depending on both state variables: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric oscillator)
- Conservative nonlinear oscillator via potential expansion: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (polynomial potential approximation)
- Piecewise stiffness / stop mechanism: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * Max(x - c2, 0) + c3 * v (contact/clearance nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (little/no v term), often as an odd function of x (e.g., x, x + x**3, sin(c*x)).
- Viscous dissipation: inclusion of a term proportional to v with negative sign (in fitted form often c*v with c < 0), producing monotone energy loss.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency (anisochrony): nonlinear stiffness terms (x**3, x**5, sin(c*x)) cause period/frequency to vary with oscillation amplitude.
- Self-excited limit cycles: nonlinear damping of the form (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v yields negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- External periodic forcing: additive sin(c*t + c) or cos(c*t + c) terms introduce resonance, entrainment, and possible quasiperiodicity/chaos when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric resonance: multiplicative time dependence on x, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, indicates stiffness modulation rather than additive forcing.
- Nonlinear drag regimes: terms like v*Abs(v) (or higher powers of v) indicate quadratic/higher-speed damping typical of aerodynamic or turbulent losses.
- Soft impacts/clearance/contact: use of Max(x-c,0), Abs(x), or strong high-order x terms indicates unilateral constraints or stiffening near boundaries.
- State-coupled dissipation: terms like x**2*v or x*v*Abs(v) reflect damping that increases with displacement amplitude (material hysteresis/geometry effects).

Rewrite the polynomial-in-\(v,x\) part:
\[
-1.0053422\,v -0.1180640\,v +0.1180640\,v x^2

\]
So GT consists of **five** independent functional pieces:
1) \(\sin(t)\) term  
2) \(\log(|v|+1)\) term  
3) \(\sin(v)\) term (non-algebraic in \(v\), not expressible by polynomials/abs/log)  
4) \(v\) term  
5) \(v x^2\) term  

Key requirement: any matching candidate must be able to represent a **\(\sin(v)\)** term with coefficient \(-0.5026711\). None of the candidates contain \(\sin(v)\) (or \(\cos(v)\)) explicitly; they only have polynomials in \(v\), \(v|v|\), \(v^3\), \(v|v|^2\), exponentials, and logs of \(|v|\) (sometimes with extra \(x\)-dependence). I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.118064*v*(1 - x²) - 1.00534*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

Expanding: `-0.118064*v + 0.118064*v*x² - 1.00534*v - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

Simplifying: `(-0.118064 - 1.00534)*v + 0.118064*v*x² - 0.502671*log(|v| + 1) + 0.342319*sin(t) - 0.502671*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v` (linear in v)
2. `v*x²` 
3. `log(|v| + 1)`
4. `sin(t)` (equivalently `cos(t + phase)`)
5. `sin(v)` — **This is critical. The GT contains `sin(v)`.**

Now I need to check which candidates contain a `sin(v)` term or something equivalent. Let me scan through all candidates:

Looking at all 50 candidates, **none of them contain `sin(v)`**. They contain terms like:
- `v*Abs(v)`, `v³`, `v*Abs(v)²`, `v**c`, `exp(...)`, `log(...)`, `x` terms, etc.

The term `-0.502671*sin(v)` is a nonlinear oscillatory function of `v`. By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, `sin(v)` cannot be represented by any combination of:
- Polynomials in `v` (`v`, `v³`, `v*|v|`, `v*|v|²`)
- `log(|v| + c)` terms
- Exponential terms in `v`
- Any `x`-dependent terms

Since `sin(v)` is linearly independent from all polynomial, logarithmic, and exponential functions, and its coefficient (-0.502671) is non-zero, **no candidate can match the GT**.

Let me verify this conclusion by checking each candidate type:

**Candidates 9-18:** Use `v*|v|`, various log terms, but no `sin(v)`. [NO MATCH]
